Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
The 39 Qawa'id of Usool al-Hidayah: An Overview
Table of contents listing 39 Hanafi legal maxims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the 39 legal maxims (qawa'id) listed in Usool al-Hidayah and explain their role as foundational principles for deriving Hanafi rulings in purification and beyond.

Core Idea
The 39 qawa'id are the axiomatic principles from which Hanafi rulings are derived.

This lesson presents the index of legal maxims (qawa'id) that form the backbone of the first volume of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are not independent rulings but tools for deriving and organizing Hanafi fatwa. By mastering them, you acquire the conceptual framework for understanding the Hidayah's treatment of purification (taharah) and other chapters.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the structure of Usool al-Hidayah
Usool al-Hidayah is a commentary on the Hidayah, but its first volume opens with a fihrist of qawa'id. Understand that these principles govern the subsequent fiqh discussions.
The maxims are numbered 1 to 39, though some numbers may be missing due to OCR issues.
2
Understand the concept of a qa'idah
A qa'idah is a general legal principle that applies to multiple cases. It is not a direct ruling but a tool for ijtihad. For example, 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (qa'idah 31) is used in many purity and evidence issues.
Refer to the key terms for 'qa'idah' and 'ghayah'.
3
Survey the 39 maxims by topic
Scan the list and group them by theme: some relate to language interpretation (6,7), others to impurity (8-11,17-19), others to general principles (12-14,21,31,37). Note the section on wells (26-32) and tayammum (39).
This survey prepares you for deeper study of each maxim in later lessons.
4
Reflect on the role of these maxims in Hanafi fiqh
Consider how a single maxim can resolve multiple cases. For instance, maxim (31) 'al-yaqeen la yazulu bi al-shakk' is applied in wudu, prayer, and contracts. These maxims are the distilled wisdom of Hanafi scholarship.
The maxims are often cited in fatwa and scholarly discourse.

Source Text

كتاب الطهارات
(1) إِنَّ الْغَايَةَ إِنْ كَانَتْ لِإِسْقَاطِ مَا وَرَاءَ تَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ الْمُغَيَّا وَإِنْ كَانَتْ بِمَنَعَةِ الْحُكْمِ لَا تَدْخُلُ
(2) إِنَّ لِلْأَكْثَرِ حُكْمُ الْكُلِّ
(3) إِنَّ الْوُضُوءَ لَا يَقَعُ قُرْبَةً إِلَّا بِالنِّيَّةِ وَلَكِنَّهُ يَقَعُ مِفْتَاحًا لِلصَّلَاةِ
(4) إِنَّ التُّرَابَ غَيْرُ مُطَهِّرٍ إِلَّا فِي حَالِ إِرَادَةِ الصَّلَاةِ
(5) إِنَّ التَّكْرَارَ لَا يَضُرُّ الْغَسْلَ بِخِلَافِ الْمَسْحِ فَإِنَّهُ يَضُرُّهُ
(6) إِنَّ الْوَاوَ لِمُطْلَقِ الْجَمْعِ بِإِجْمَاعِ أَهْلِ اللُّغَةِ
(7) إِنَّ كَلِمَةَ مَا عَامَّةٌ
فصل في نواقض الوضوء
(8) إِنَّ خُرُوجَ النَّجَاسَةِ مُؤَثِّرٌ فِي زَوَالِ الطَّهَارَةِ
(9) إِنَّ مَا لَا يَكُونُ حَدَثًا لَا يَكُونُ نَجَسًا
(10) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَزِجًا لَا تَتَخَلَّلُهُ النَّجَاسَةُ
(11) إِنَّ الْمِعْدَةَ لَيْسَتْ بِمَحَلِّ الدَّمِ
(12) إِنَّ الثَّابِتَ عَادَةً كَالْمُتَيَقَّنِ بِهِ
(13) إِنَّ الْحَرَجَ مَدْفُوعٌ شَرْعًا
(14) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَخْفِيًّا أُقِيمَ السَّبَبُ مَقَامَهُ
باب الماء الذي يجوز به الوضوء وما لا يجوز به
(15) إِنَّ الْمُطْلَقَ إِذَا أُطْلِقَ يُرَادُ بِهِ فَرْدٌ كَامِلٌ
(16) إِنَّ اسْمَ الشَّيْءِ إِذَا كَانَ بَاقِيًا يَبْقَى حُكْمُهُ
(17) إِنَّ الْحُرْمَةَ لَيْسَتْ مِنْ ضَرُورَتِهَا النَّجَاسَةُ
(18) إِنَّ النَّجَاسَةَ إِذَا كَانَتْ فِي مَعْدِنِهَا لَا يُعْطَى لَهَا حُكْمُ النَّجَاسَةِ
(19) إِنَّ مُلَاقَاةَ الطَّاهِرِ الطَّاهِرَ لَا تُوجِبُ النَّجَسَ
(20) إِنَّ اخْتِلَافَ الْعُلَمَاءِ يُورِثُ تَخْفِيفًا
(21) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا
(22) إِنَّ مَا يَنْتَفِعُ بِهِ فَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِنَجِسِ الْعَيْنِ
(23) إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ إِذَا حَصَلَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ غَيْرِهِ
(24) إِنَّ مَا يَطْهُرُ جِلْدُهُ بِالدِّبَاغِ يَطْهُرُ بِالزَّكَاةِ
(25) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ حَيَاةٌ لَا يَحِلُّهُ الْمَوْتُ
فصل في البئر
(26) إِنَّ مَسَائِلَ الْآبَارِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى اتِّبَاعِ الْآثَارِ دُونَ الْقِيَاسِ
(27) إِنَّ الْقَلِيلَ جُعِلَ عَفْوًا لِلضَّرُورَةِ
(28) إِنَّ بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا
(29) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِيَ بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِنْدَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ
(30) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ
(31) إِنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ بِالشَّكِّ
(32) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ سَبَبًا ظَاهِرًا يُحَالُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ
فصل في الآسار وغيرها
(33) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَوْلِدُهُمَا وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ صَاحِبِهِ
(34) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّدَ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ
(35) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُونَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأَوْلَى
(36) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّدَ مِنْ نَجِسٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا نَجِسٌ
(37) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِي الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالْحُرْمَةِ يُورِثُ الشَّكَّ وَكَذَا اخْتِلَافُ الصَّحَابَةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنْهُمْ
(38) إِنَّ الْحَدِيثَ إِذَا كَانَ مَشْهُورًا وَعَمِلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ يَصِحُّ بِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ
باب التيمم
(39) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ
Book of Purification. (1) Indeed the limit [ghayah], if it is for nullifying what is beyond, enters under the limited; if it is for the prevention of the ruling, it does not enter. (2) Indeed the majority has the ruling of the whole. (3) Indeed ablution is not valid as worship except with intention, but it is a key for prayer. (4) Indeed earth is not purifying except in the case of intending prayer. (5) Indeed repetition does not harm washing, contrary to wiping for it harms it. (6) Indeed the letter waw is for absolute conjunction by consensus of linguists. (7) Indeed the word 'ma' is general. Section on nullifiers of ablution. (8) Indeed the exit of impurity effects the removal of purity. (9) Indeed what is not a hadath is not impure. (10) Indeed a thing if it is sticky, impurity does not permeate it. (11) Indeed the stomach is not a place for blood. (12) Indeed what is established by custom is like what is certain. (13) Indeed hardship is repelled by law. (14) Indeed a thing when it is hidden, the cause is put in its place. Chapter on water with which ablution is permissible and what is not permissible with it. (15) Indeed the absolute when unqualified refers to a complete individual. (16) Indeed the name of a thing if it remains, its ruling remains. (17) Indeed prohibition does not necessarily entail impurity. (18) Indeed impurity when it is in its origin, no ruling of impurity is given to it. (19) Indeed the contact of pure with pure does not necessitate impurity. (20) Indeed the disagreement of scholars leads to leniency. (21) Indeed a thing when established by necessity is limited to its extent. (22) Indeed what is beneficial is not an impure substance. (23) Indeed the objective when attained by something, there is no meaning to stipulating another. (24) Indeed what its skin is purified by tanning, it is purified by zakah. (25) Indeed a thing in which there is no life, death does not affect it. Section on the well. (26) Indeed the issues of wells are based on following traditions, not analogy. (27) Indeed a small amount is treated as excused due to necessity. (28) Indeed the urine of what is eaten for its meat is pure according to Muhammad, and impure according to the two [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad]. (29) Indeed treatment with a prohibited substance is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. (30) Indeed a thing when it equals another takes its ruling. (31) Indeed certainty is not removed by doubt. (32) Indeed a thing if it has an apparent cause, it is attributed to it. Section on traces and other things. (33) Indeed a thing when their origin and source are one, one of them takes the ruling of the other. (34) Indeed what is produced from pure is also pure. (35) Indeed a thing when it has a ruling, what is below it enters that ruling all the more. (36) Indeed what is produced from impure is also impure. (37) Indeed the conflict of evidence in permissibility and prohibition causes doubt, likewise the disagreement of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. (38) Indeed a hadith if it is well-known and the Companions acted upon it, increase upon the Book is valid by it. Chapter on tayammum. (39) Indeed inability when it is established as real, it must be considered.
Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents (fihrist) of the first volume of Usool al-Hidayah, listing the legal maxims (qawa'id) that form the foundational principles of the Hidayah. The book is organized by chapters starting with Taharah (Purification). Each maxim is stated concisely and will be elaborated in the main text. The numbering spans from (1) to (39), though some numbers are missing in the OCR. These maxims cover topics such as the scope of limits (ghayah), the effect of majority, the role of intention in wudu, the definition of impurity, the treatment of wells, and the use of analogy (qiyas) versus tradition (athar). They are essential for understanding the Hanafi methodology in deriving rulings. The teacher should note that these are foundational for the entire work and many are discussed in the context of primary evidence (adillah).

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'idah): A legal maxim or principle that governs multiple cases in Hanafi fiqh.
الغاية (al-ghayah): The limit or endpoint mentioned in a legal ruling, e.g., 'until the neck'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which principle states that certainty is not overridden by doubt?
A) Principle (31): إِنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ بِالشَّكِّ
B) Principle (12): إِنَّ الثَّابِتَ عَادَةً كَالْمُتَيَقَّنِ بِهِ
C) Principle (13): إِنَّ الْحَرَجَ مَدْفُوعٌ شَرْعًا
D) Principle (21): إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا

Key Takeaway
The 39 qawa'id of Usool al-Hidayah are essential tools for deriving Hanafi rulings; they are not rulings themselves but general principles that ensure consistency across fiqh.

Module 2 · Lesson 2

Taharah — Purification
beginner
10 min
The Foundational Maxims: Disagreement, Necessity, Benefit, and Objective
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state and apply four key Hanafi legal maxims: ikhtilaf brings ease, necessity measures extent, benefit implies purity, and achieving objective suffices.

Core Idea
Ikhtilaf brings ease; necessity dictates its own measure.

This lesson introduces the first set of Hanafi legal maxims from Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims form the bedrock of Hanafi juristic reasoning, providing flexibility and practicality. They remind us that scholarly disagreement is a mercy, and that rules adapt to necessity and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Recite the maxim
Read each maxim aloud in Arabic, noting the introductory phrase 'إِنَّ'.
Memorization anchor: repeat to internalize.
2
Translate and understand the literal meaning
Render each maxim into clear English. Clarify key terms like 'ضرورة' (necessity) and 'عفو' (excused).
Literal understanding precedes legal application.
3
Identify the legal implication
Explain the fiqh consequence: disagreement allows for multiple valid rulings; necessity enlarges permissions; benefit indicates purity; achievement of objective removes need for extra conditions.
Each maxim has a direct impact on ruling derivation.
4
Apply to a simple case
For maxim 20: Two scholars differ on a matter, so the community may follow either. For maxim 21: If a person is forced to eat carrion, only the amount needed is permissible.
Practical application solidifies understanding.

اصول ہدایہ جلد اول (٢٠) إِنَّ اِخْتِلَافَ الْعُلَمَاءِ يُورِثُ تَخْفِيفًا (۲۱) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا (٢١) إِنَّ مَا يَنْتَفِعُ بِهِ فَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِنَجَسِ الْعَيْنِ (۲۳) إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ إِذَا حَصَلَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ غَيْرِهِ (۲۴) إِنَّ مَا يَطْهُرُ جِلْدُهُ بِالدِّبَاعَ يَطْهُرُ بِالزَّكَاةِ (۲۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ حَيَاةٌ لَا يَحِلُّهُ الْمَوْتُ فصل في البئر (٢٦) إِنَّ مَسَائِلَ الْآبَارِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى اتِّبَاعِ الْآثَارِ دُونَ الْقِيَاسِ (۲۷) إِنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ جُعِلَ عَفُوا لِلضَّرُورَةِ (۲۸) إِنَّ بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا (۲۹) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِى بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ (٣٠) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ (۳۱) إِنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ بالشَّكِ (۳۲) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ سَبَبًا ظَاهِرًا يُحَالُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ فصل في الآسار وغيرها (۳۳) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَوْلَدُهُمَا وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ صَاحِبِهِ (۳۴) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ (۳۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُوْنَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأَوْلَى (٣٦) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّدَ مِنْ نَجِسٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا نَجِسٌ (۳۷) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِي الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالْحُرُمَةِ يُورِثُ الشَّكَ وَكَذَا اِخْتِلَافُ الصَّحَابَةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عنهم (۳۸) إِنَّ الْحَدِيث إِذَا كَانَ مَشْهُورًا وَعَمِلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ يَصِحُ بِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ باب التيمم (۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ (۴۰) إِنَّ النَّائِمَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (۴۱) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ (۴۲) إِنَّ غَالِبَ الرَّأْى كَالْمُتَحَقَّق (۴۳) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَزُولُ حُكْمُهُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ (۴۴) لَا قُدْرَةَ بِدُونِ الْعِلْمِ (۴۵) إِنَّ الضَّرَرَ مُسْقِط باب المسح على الخفين (٢٦) إِنَّ مَا هُوَ مَعْدُولٌ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ يُرَاعَى جَمِيعُ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ الشَّرُعُ (۴۷) إِنَّ رُخْصَةَ السَّفَرِ لَا تَبْقَى بِدُونِهِ باب الحيض والاستحاضة (۴۸) إِنَّ تَقْدِيرَ الشَّرُعَ يَمْنَعُ إِلْحَاقَ غَيْرِهِ بِهِ باب الأنجاس وتطهيرها (۴۹) إِنَّ الْمَائِعَ قَالِعٌ (۵۰) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَتْ نَجَاسَةٌ بِدَلِيْلٍ مَقْطُوعِ بِهِ تَكُونُ مُعَلَّظَةٌ (۵۱) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ النَّصَّيْنِ فِى نَجَاسَةِ شَيْءٍ يُوجِبُ التَّخْفِيفَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كتاب الصلاة باب الأذان (۵۲) إِنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْأَذَانِ مَشْرُوعٌ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ (۵۳) إِنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ (۵۴) إِنَّ الأَدَانَ لِلاِسْتِحْضَارِ وَالْإِقَامَةَ لِإِعْلَامِ الْإِفْتِتَاحِ باب شروط الصلاة (۵۵) إِنَّ الرُّبُعَ يَحْكِي حِكَايَةَ الْكَمَالِ (۵۶) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنَّمَا يُوصَفُ بِالْكَبْرَةِ إِذَا كَانَ مَا يُقَابِلُهُ أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ (۵۷) إِنَّ رُبعَ الشَّيْءِ يَقُومُ مَقَامَ كُلِهِ (۵۸) إِنَّ تَرَكَ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى خَلْفِ لَا يَكُونُ تَرْعًا
Principles of Hidayah Volume 1 (20) Indeed, disagreement of scholars brings ease. (21) Indeed, when a matter is established by necessity, it is measured by its extent. (21) Indeed, that which is benefited from is not intrinsically impure. (23) Indeed, when the objective is achieved by something, there is no meaning to stipulating something else. (24) Indeed, that whose skin is purified by tanning is purified by zakat. (25) Indeed, a thing in which there is no life is not decomposed by death. Chapter on the Well (26) Indeed, the issues of wells are based on following traditions, not analogy. (27) Indeed, a small amount is excused due to necessity. (28) Indeed, the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure according to Muhammad, and impure according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa). (29) Indeed, treatment with what is forbidden is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. (30) Indeed, when a thing equals another, it takes its ruling. (31) Indeed, certainty is not removed by doubt. (32) Indeed, a thing, if it has an apparent cause, it is attributed to it. Chapter on Traces and Others (33) Indeed, when two things share the same origin and source, one takes the ruling of the other. (34) Indeed, what is generated from a pure thing is also pure. (35) Indeed, when a thing has a ruling, what is less than it enters that ruling by greater reason. (36) Indeed, what is generated from an impure thing is also impure. (37) Indeed, conflict of evidences regarding permissibility and prohibition brings doubt, and likewise disagreement of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. (38) Indeed, when a hadith is well-known and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to add to the Quran by it. Chapter on Tayammum (39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered. (40) Indeed, a sleeping person is considered able in estimation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (41) Indeed, that which is a means of purification must itself be pure. (42) Indeed, predominant opinion is like certainty. (43) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, its ruling does not cease except by a certainty like it. (44) No ability without knowledge. (45) Indeed, harm is removable. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffain (46) Indeed, what is deviated from analogy is observed according to all that the Law has brought. (47) Indeed, the concession of travel does not remain without it. Chapter on Menstruation and Istihadah (48) Indeed, the determination of the Law prevents attaching others to it. Chapter on Impurities and Their Purification (49) Indeed, a liquid is [a] remover. (50) Indeed, when impurity is established by a definitive proof, it is intensified. (51) Indeed, conflict of two texts regarding the impurity of something necessitates ease according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him. Book of Prayer Chapter on Adhan (52) Indeed, repetition of the adhan is legislated but not of the iqamah. (53) Indeed, the adhan is for notification. (54) Indeed, the adhan is for summoning and the iqamah is for announcing the commencement. Chapter on Conditions of Prayer (55) Indeed, the quarter narrates the narration of completion. (56) Indeed, a thing is only described as abundant when its opposite is less than it. (57) Indeed, a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole. (58) Indeed, leaving a thing to the back is not a leaving.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyyah) from the beginning of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are foundational principles that guide the derivation of rulings in various chapters of fiqh. The author presents them succinctly, often without proof, as they are axiomatic in the Hanafi school. The maxims cover diverse topics: disagreement of scholars brings ease (20), necessity dictates extent (21), benefit implies purity (22), achieving objective obviates extra conditions (23), tanning purifies skin (24), lifeless things do not decompose (25), well issues follow tradition not analogy (26), small amounts are excused (27), urine of edible animals is pure according to Imam Muhammad but impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (28), treatment with forbidden substances is prohibited (29), equality in cause gives same ruling (30), certainty not removed by doubt (31), things attributed to apparent cause (32), common origin gives same ruling (33), pure begets pure (34), inclusion by greater priority (35), impure begets impure (36), conflicting evidence on Halal and Haram brings doubt (37), well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran (38), established incapacity must be considered (39), sleeper considered capable in estimation (40), purification tools must be pure (41), predominant opinion like certainty (42), incapacity ruling only removed by certainty (43), no ability without knowledge (44), harm is removable (45), deviation from analogy follows textual detail (46), travel concession depends on travel (47), legal determinations prevent analogy (48), liquid removes impurity (49), impurity established by decisive proof is severe (50), conflicting texts on impurity bring ease (51). In the Book of Prayer: adhan repetition is legislated but not iqamah (52), adhan is for notification (53), adhan for summoning, iqamah for commencement (54), quarter narrates completion (55), abundance defined by comparison (56), quarter stands for whole (57), leaving to back is not leaving (58). These maxims are used by Hanafi jurists to resolve new cases analogically.

Key Terms
قاعدة فقهية (qāʿida fiqhiyya): A legal maxim that encapsulates a general principle of Hanafi fiqh.
عفو (ʿafw): Legally excused or overlooked, referring to small amounts that are tolerated.
تقيدر الشرع (taqdīr al-sharʿ): Specific determinations by Islamic law that prevent analogical extension.
ضرورة (ḍarūra): Necessity that permits normally prohibited acts, measured by its extent.
اختلاف العلماء (ikhtilāf al-ʿulamāʾ): Scholarly disagreement, viewed in Hanafi as a source of ease.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim (20) 'إِنَّ اِخْتِلَافَ الْعُلَمَاءِ يُورِثُ تَخْفِيفًا', what is the effect of scholarly disagreement?
A) It creates confusion and must be avoided.
B) It brings ease (takhfif).
C) It leads to the invalidity of both opinions.
D) It requires following the majority opinion.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi legal maxims provide flexible yet principled guidance for deriving rulings, with ikhtilaf as a mercy and necessity as a measured allowance.

Module 2 · Lesson 3

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Maxims on Purity and Impurity
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi maxims regarding well water, small amounts of impurities, urine of edible animals, and the prohibition of treating with forbidden substances.

Core Idea
Small impurities are excused; well rulings follow tradition, not analogy.

This lesson focuses on maxims related to taharah and najasah. The Hanafi school makes nuanced distinctions: small amounts of impurity are overlooked, but the urine of edible animals is a point of disagreement among the imams. Treatment with forbidden substances is generally prohibited, and well issues are resolved by following transmitted reports rather than analogical reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject of each maxim
Each maxim addresses a specific purity issue: wells, small amounts, urine, treatment.
Recognize the chapter context (Taharah).
2
Understand the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Maxim 28 shows disagreement: Muhammad says urine of edible animals is pure; Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf say it is impure.
Note the mufta bihi is the view of the two (the majority).
3
Apply the maxim on small amounts
Maxim 27: 'A small amount is excused due to necessity.' For example, a drop of blood on clothes less than a dirham is forgiven.
The quantity threshold is defined by custom or text.
4
Contrast with well issues
Maxim 26: Well issues are based on following traditions (athar), not qiyas. This means one must know specific hadith rulings for wells, not derive by analogy.
This is a deviation from general principle of qiyas.

Source Text

اصول ہدایہ جلد اول (٢٠) إِنَّ اِخْتِلَافَ الْعُلَمَاءِ يُورِثُ تَخْفِيفًا (۲۱) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا (٢١) إِنَّ مَا يَنْتَفِعُ بِهِ فَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِنَجَسِ الْعَيْنِ (۲۳) إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ إِذَا حَصَلَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ غَيْرِهِ (۲۴) إِنَّ مَا يَطْهُرُ جِلْدُهُ بِالدِّبَاعَ يَطْهُرُ بِالزَّكَاةِ (۲۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ حَيَاةٌ لَا يَحِلُّهُ الْمَوْتُ فصل في البئر (٢٦) إِنَّ مَسَائِلَ الْآبَارِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى اتِّبَاعِ الْآثَارِ دُونَ الْقِيَاسِ (۲۷) إِنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ جُعِلَ عَفُوا لِلضَّرُورَةِ (۲۸) إِنَّ بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا (۲۹) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِى بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ (٣٠) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ (۳۱) إِنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ بالشَّكِ (۳۲) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ سَبَبًا ظَاهِرًا يُحَالُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ فصل في الآسار وغيرها (۳۳) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَوْلَدُهُمَا وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ صَاحِبِهِ (۳۴) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ (۳۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُوْنَهُ يَدْخُلُ Key Terms
بئر (biʾr): Well; its rulings are based on transmitted reports not analogy.
عفو (ʿafw): Legally excused small impurity.
محرم (muḥarram): Forbidden substance; treatment with it is generally prohibited.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
14 min
Maxims on Reasoning: Certainty, Cause, Priority, and Generation
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply maxims of certainty, attribution to cause, priority, and purity/impurity of generated things.

Core Idea
Certainty prevails over doubt; causes govern effects; pure begets pure.

This lesson covers logical and inferential maxims that guide juristic reasoning. The famous maxim 'certainty is not removed by doubt' (31) is fundamental in fiqh. Others establish that when two things share the same origin, they share rulings, and that a thing inherits the ruling of its generator (pure from pure, impure from impure). Priority (a fortiori) reasoning is also included.

Guided Path
1
Understand the certainty maxim
Maxim 31: If one is certain of wudu but doubts a nullifier, the certainty remains. This is used in many fiqh issues.
This is a universal principle across madhhabs, but Hanafis apply it strictly.
2
Learn attribution to cause
Maxim 32: Things are attributed to their apparent cause. For example, if water becomes impure, the cause (e.g., falling najis) is considered.
Helps in identifying the origin of impurity.
3
Apply the generation principle
Maxim 34 and 36: Pure generates pure, impure generates impure. E.g., milk from a pure animal is pure; wine vinegar from wine? but it changes ruling?
There are exceptions; vinegar from wine is pure by transformation (istihalah).
4
Recognize a fortiori reasoning
Maxim 35: If a thing has a ruling, what is less than it falls under that ruling by greater reason. E.g., if touching impurity requires washing, then swallowing it is more serious.
This is qiyas jali (evident analogy).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اصول ہدایہ جلد اول (٢٠) إِنَّ اِخْتِلَافَ الْعُلَمَاءِ يُورِثُ تَخْفِيفًا (۲۱) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَ بِالضَّرُورَةِ يَتَقَدَّرُ بِقَدْرِهَا (٢١) إِنَّ مَا يَنْتَفِعُ بِهِ فَهُوَ لَيْسَ بِنَجَسِ الْعَيْنِ (۲۳) إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ إِذَا حَصَلَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ غَيْرِهِ (۲۴) إِنَّ مَا يَطْهُرُ جِلْدُهُ بِالدِّبَاعَ يَطْهُرُ بِالزَّكَاةِ (۲۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ فِيهِ حَيَاةٌ لَا يَحِلُّهُ الْمَوْتُ فصل في البئر (٢٦) إِنَّ مَسَائِلَ الْآبَارِ مَبْنِيَّةٌ عَلَى اتِّبَاعِ الْآثَارِ دُونَ الْقِيَاسِ (۲۷) إِنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ جُعِلَ عَفُوا لِلضَّرُورَةِ (۲۸) إِنَّ بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا (۲۹) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِى بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ (٣٠) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ حُكْمَهُ (۳۱) إِنَّ الْيَقِينَ لَا يَزُولُ بالشَّكِ (۳۲) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنْ كَانَ لَهُ سَبَبًا ظَاهِرًا يُحَالُ بِهِ عَلَيْهِ فصل في الآسار وغيرها (۳۳) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ مَوْلَدُهُمَا وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ صَاحِبِهِ (۳۴) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ (۳۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُوْنَهُ يَدْخُلُ فِي ذَلِكَ الْحُكْمِ بِالْأَوْلَى (٣٦) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّدَ مِنْ نَجِسٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا نَجِسٌ (۳۷) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ الْأَدِلَّةِ فِي الْإِبَاحَةِ وَالْحُرُمَةِ يُورِثُ الشَّكَ وَكَذَا اِخْتِلَافُ الصَّحَابَةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عنهم (۳۸) إِنَّ الْحَدِيث إِذَا كَانَ مَشْهُورًا وَعَمِلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ يَصِحُ بِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ باب التيمم (۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ (۴۰) إِنَّ النَّائِمَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (۴۱) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ (۴۲) إِنَّ غَالِبَ الرَّأْى كَالْمُتَحَقَّق (۴۳) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَزُولُ حُكْمُهُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ (۴۴) لَا قُدْرَةَ بِدُونِ الْعِلْمِ (۴۵) إِنَّ الضَّرَرَ مُسْقِط باب المسح على الخفين (٢٦) إِنَّ مَا هُوَ مَعْدُولٌ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ يُرَاعَى جَمِيعُ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ الشَّرُعُ (۴۷) إِنَّ رُخْصَةَ السَّفَرِ لَا تَبْقَى بِدُونِهِ باب الحيض والاستحاضة (۴۸) إِنَّ تَقْدِيرَ الشَّرُعَ يَمْنَعُ إِلْحَاقَ غَيْرِهِ بِهِ باب الأنجاس وتطهيرها (۴۹) إِنَّ الْمَائِعَ قَالِعٌ (۵۰) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَتْ نَجَاسَةٌ بِدَلِيْلٍ مَقْطُوعِ بِهِ تَكُونُ مُعَلَّظَةٌ (۵۱) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ النَّصَّيْنِ فِى نَجَاسَةِ شَيْءٍ يُوجِبُ التَّخْفِيفَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كتاب الصلاة باب الأذان (۵۲) إِنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْأَذَانِ مَشْرُوعٌ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ (۵۳) إِنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ (۵۴) إِنَّ الأَدَانَ لِلاِسْتِحْضَارِ وَالْإِقَامَةَ لِإِعْلَامِ الْإِفْتِتَاحِ باب شروط الصلاة (۵۵) إِنَّ الرُّبُعَ يَحْكِي حِكَايَةَ الْكَمَالِ (۵۶) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنَّمَا يُوصَفُ بِالْكَبْرَةِ إِذَا كَانَ مَا يُقَابِلُهُ أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ (۵۷) إِنَّ رُبعَ الشَّيْءِ يَقُومُ مَقَامَ كُلِهِ (۵۸) إِنَّ تَرَكَ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى خَلْفِ لَا يَكُونُ تَرْعًا
Principles of Hidayah Volume 1 (20) Indeed, disagreement of scholars brings ease. (21) Indeed, when a matter is established by necessity, it is measured by its extent. (21) Indeed, that which is benefited from is not intrinsically impure. (23) Indeed, when the objective is achieved by something, there is no meaning to stipulating something else. (24) Indeed, that whose skin is purified by tanning is purified by zakat. (25) Indeed, a thing in which there is no life is not decomposed by death. Chapter on the Well (26) Indeed, the issues of wells are based on following traditions, not analogy. (27) Indeed, a small amount is excused due to necessity. (28) Indeed, the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure according to Muhammad, and impure according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa). (29) Indeed, treatment with what is forbidden is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. (30) Indeed, when a thing equals another, it takes its ruling. (31) Indeed, certainty is not removed by doubt. (32) Indeed, a thing, if it has an apparent cause, it is attributed to it. Chapter on Traces and Others (33) Indeed, when two things share the same origin and source, one takes the ruling of the other. (34) Indeed, what is generated from a pure thing is also pure. (35) Indeed, when a thing has a ruling, what is less than it enters that ruling by greater reason. (36) Indeed, what is generated from an impure thing is also impure. (37) Indeed, conflict of evidences regarding permissibility and prohibition brings doubt, and likewise disagreement of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. (38) Indeed, when a hadith is well-known and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to add to the Quran by it. Chapter on Tayammum (39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered. (40) Indeed, a sleeping person is considered able in estimation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (41) Indeed, that which is a means of purification must itself be pure. (42) Indeed, predominant opinion is like certainty. (43) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, its ruling does not cease except by a certainty like it. (44) No ability without knowledge. (45) Indeed, harm is removable. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffain (46) Indeed, what is deviated from analogy is observed according to all that the Law has brought. (47) Indeed, the concession of travel does not remain without it. Chapter on Menstruation and Istihadah (48) Indeed, the determination of the Law prevents attaching others to it. Chapter on Impurities and Their Purification (49) Indeed, a liquid is [a] remover. (50) Indeed, when impurity is established by a definitive proof, it is intensified. (51) Indeed, conflict of two texts regarding the impurity of something necessitates ease according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him. Book of Prayer Chapter on Adhan (52) Indeed, repetition of the adhan is legislated but not of the iqamah. (53) Indeed, the adhan is for notification. (54) Indeed, the adhan is for summoning and the iqamah is for announcing the commencement. Chapter on Conditions of Prayer (55) Indeed, the quarter narrates the narration of completion. (56) Indeed, a thing is only described as abundant when its opposite is less than it. (57) Indeed, a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole. (58) Indeed, leaving a thing to the back is not a leaving.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyyah) from the beginning of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are foundational principles that guide the derivation of rulings in various chapters of fiqh. The author presents them succinctly, often without proof, as they are axiomatic in the Hanafi school. The maxims cover diverse topics: disagreement of scholars brings ease (20), necessity dictates extent (21), benefit implies purity (22), achieving objective obviates extra conditions (23), tanning purifies skin (24), lifeless things do not decompose (25), well issues follow tradition not analogy (26), small amounts are excused (27), urine of edible animals is pure according to Imam Muhammad but impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (28), treatment with forbidden substances is prohibited (29), equality in cause gives same ruling (30), certainty not removed by doubt (31), things attributed to apparent cause (32), common origin gives same ruling (33), pure begets pure (34), inclusion by greater priority (35), impure begets impure (36), conflicting evidence on Halal and Haram brings doubt (37), well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran (38), established incapacity must be considered (39), sleeper considered capable in estimation (40), purification tools must be pure (41), predominant opinion like certainty (42), incapacity ruling only removed by certainty (43), no ability without knowledge (44), harm is removable (45), deviation from analogy follows textual detail (46), travel concession depends on travel (47), legal determinations prevent analogy (48), liquid removes impurity (49), impurity established by decisive proof is severe (50), conflicting texts on impurity bring ease (51). In the Book of Prayer: adhan repetition is legislated but not iqamah (52), adhan is for notification (53), adhan for summoning, iqamah for commencement (54), quarter narrates completion (55), abundance defined by comparison (56), quarter stands for whole (57), leaving to back is not leaving (58). These maxims are used by Hanafi jurists to resolve new cases analogically.

Key Terms
يقين (yaqīn): Certainty; legal state that is not removed by doubt.
شك (shakk): Doubt; does not override established certainty.
تولد (tawallud): Generation; byproduct inherits the ruling of the origin.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim 31, if a person is certain they have performed wudu but later doubts whether they broke it, what is the ruling?
A) They must repeat wudu.
B) Their wudu remains valid.
C) They must perform tayammum.
D) They should combine two prayers.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi reasoning relies on certainty, causation, and generation principles to maintain consistency and predictability in rulings.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
12 min
Maxims on Evidence and Dispute
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply maxims on conflicting evidence, acting upon well-known hadith, and the effect of Companion disagreement.

Core Idea
Conflicting evidence on Halal/Haram creates doubt; well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran.

This lesson deals with how Hanafi jurists handle conflicts in evidence. Maxim 37 states that when evidences conflict regarding permissibility and prohibition, the result is doubt, leading to caution. Maxim 38 addresses the authority of well-known hadith (mashhur) that the Companions practiced, which can supplement the Quran. This is a key principle in Hanafi usul.

Guided Path
1
Understand the effect of conflicting evidence
Maxim 37: If one evidence says halal and another says haram, they are considered contradictory, creating doubt. In such cases, the default is caution.
This does not mean both are automatically invalid; one may be stronger.
2
Learn the weight of Companion practice
Maxim 38: A hadith that is mashhur (well-known, not necessarily mutawatir) and acted upon by the Companions can be used to add a rule not explicitly in the Quran.
This is a Hanafi principle that gives more power to sunnah than some other schools.
3
Contrast with mutawatir and ahad
The maxim specifically says 'mashhur and acted upon by the Companions', which elevates its authority.
This is used to justify additions like the prohibition of marrying a woman and her aunt simultaneously.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

الْعَيْنِ (۲۳) إِنَّ الْمَقْصُودَ إِذَا حَصَلَ بِشَيْءٍ فَلَا مَعْنَى لِاشْتِرَاطِ غَيْرِهِ (۲۴) إِنَّ مَا يَطْهُرُ جِلْدُهُ بِالدِّبَاعَ يَطْهُرُ بِالزَّكَاةِ (۲۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنْ بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا (۲۹) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِى بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ (٣٠) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ وَمَأْخَذُهُمَا وَاحِدًا يَأْخُذُ أَحَدُهُمَا حُكْمَ صَاحِبِهِ (۳۴) إِنَّ مَا تَوَلَّذِ مِنْ طَاهِرٍ فَهُوَ أَيْضًا طَاهِرٌ (۳۵) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا كَانَ لَهُ حُكْمٌ فَمَا هُوَ دُوْنَهُ يَدْخُلُ حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ (۴۰) إِنَّ النَّائِمَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (۴۱) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ (۴۲) إِنَّ غَالِبَ الرَّأْى كَالْمُتَحَقَّق (۴۳) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيقَةٌ فَلَا يَزُولُ حُكْمُهُ إِلَّا بِيَقِينِ مِثْلِهِ (۴۴) لَا قُدْرَةَ بِدُونِ الْعِلْمِ (۴۵) إِنَّ الضَّرَرَ مُسْقِط باب المسح على الخفين (٢٦) إِنَّ مَا هُوَ مَعْدُولٌ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ يُرَاعَى جَمِيعُ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ الشَّرُعُ (۴۷) إِنَّ رُخْصَةَ السَّفَرِ لَا تَبْقَى بِدُونِهِ باب الحيض والاستحاضة (۴۸) إِنَّ تَقْدِيرَ الشَّرُعَ يَمْنَعُ إِلْحَاقَ غَيْرِهِ بِهِ باب الأنجاس وتطهيرها (۴۹) إِنَّ الْمَائِعَ قَالِعٌ (۵۰) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا ثَبَتَتْ نَجَاسَةٌ بِدَلِيْلٍ مَقْطُوعِ بِهِ تَكُونُ مُعَلَّظَةٌ (۵۱) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ النَّصَّيْنِ فِى نَجَاسَةِ شَيْءٍ يُوجِبُ التَّخْفِيفَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كتاب الصلاة باب الأذان (۵۲) إِنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْأَذَانِ مَشْرُوعٌ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ (۵۳) إِنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ (۵۴) إِنَّ الأَدَانَ لِلاِسْتِحْضَارِ وَالْإِقَامَةَ لِإِعْلَامِ الْإِفْتِتَاحِ باب شروط الصلاة (۵۵) إِنَّ الرُّبُعَ يَحْكِي حِكَايَةَ الْكَمَالِ (۵۶) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنَّمَا يُوصَفُ بِالْكَبْرَةِ إِذَا كَانَ مَا يُقَابِلُهُ أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ (۵۷) إِنَّ رُبعَ الشَّيْءِ يَقُومُ مَقَامَ كُلِهِ (۵۸) إِنَّ تَرَكَ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى خَلْفِ لَا يَكُونُ تَرْعًا
Principles of Hidayah Volume 1 (20) Indeed, disagreement of scholars brings ease. (21) Indeed, when a matter is established by necessity, it is measured by its extent. (21) Indeed, that which is benefited from is not intrinsically impure. (23) Indeed, when the objective is achieved by something, there is no meaning to stipulating something else. (24) Indeed, that whose skin is purified by tanning is purified by zakat. (25) Indeed, a thing in which there is no life is not decomposed by death. Chapter on the Well (26) Indeed, the issues of wells are based on following traditions, not analogy. (27) Indeed, a small amount is excused due to necessity. (28) Indeed, the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure according to Muhammad, and impure according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa). (29) Indeed, treatment with what is forbidden is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. (30) Indeed, when a thing equals another, it takes its ruling. (31) Indeed, certainty is not removed by doubt. (32) Indeed, a thing, if it has an apparent cause, it is attributed to it. Chapter on Traces and Others (33) Indeed, when two things share the same origin and source, one takes the ruling of the other. (34) Indeed, what is generated from a pure thing is also pure. (35) Indeed, when a thing has a ruling, what is less than it enters that ruling by greater reason. (36) Indeed, what is generated from an impure thing is also impure. (37) Indeed, conflict of evidences regarding permissibility and prohibition brings doubt, and likewise disagreement of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. (38) Indeed, when a hadith is well-known and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to add to the Quran by it. Chapter on Tayammum (39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered. (40) Indeed, a sleeping person is considered able in estimation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (41) Indeed, that which is a means of purification must itself be pure. (42) Indeed, predominant opinion is like certainty. (43) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, its ruling does not cease except by a certainty like it. (44) No ability without knowledge. (45) Indeed, harm is removable. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffain (46) Indeed, what is deviated from analogy is observed according to all that the Law has brought. (47) Indeed, the concession of travel does not remain without it. Chapter on Menstruation and Istihadah (48) Indeed, the determination of the Law prevents attaching others to it. Chapter on Impurities and Their Purification (49) Indeed, a liquid is [a] remover. (50) Indeed, when impurity is established by a definitive proof, it is intensified. (51) Indeed, conflict of two texts regarding the impurity of something necessitates ease according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him. Book of Prayer Chapter on Adhan (52) Indeed, repetition of the adhan is legislated but not of the iqamah. (53) Indeed, the adhan is for notification. (54) Indeed, the adhan is for summoning and the iqamah is for announcing the commencement. Chapter on Conditions of Prayer (55) Indeed, the quarter narrates the narration of completion. (56) Indeed, a thing is only described as abundant when its opposite is less than it. (57) Indeed, a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole. (58) Indeed, leaving a thing to the back is not a leaving.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyyah) from the beginning of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are foundational principles that guide the derivation of rulings in various chapters of fiqh. The author presents them succinctly, often without proof, as they are axiomatic in the Hanafi school. The maxims cover diverse topics: disagreement of scholars brings ease (20), necessity dictates extent (21), benefit implies purity (22), achieving objective obviates extra conditions (23), tanning purifies skin (24), lifeless things do not decompose (25), well issues follow tradition not analogy (26), small amounts are excused (27), urine of edible animals is pure according to Imam Muhammad but impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (28), treatment with forbidden substances is prohibited (29), equality in cause gives same ruling (30), certainty not removed by doubt (31), things attributed to apparent cause (32), common origin gives same ruling (33), pure begets pure (34), inclusion by greater priority (35), impure begets impure (36), conflicting evidence on Halal and Haram brings doubt (37), well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran (38), established incapacity must be considered (39), sleeper considered capable in estimation (40), purification tools must be pure (41), predominant opinion like certainty (42), incapacity ruling only removed by certainty (43), no ability without knowledge (44), harm is removable (45), deviation from analogy follows textual detail (46), travel concession depends on travel (47), legal determinations prevent analogy (48), liquid removes impurity (49), impurity established by decisive proof is severe (50), conflicting texts on impurity bring ease (51). In the Book of Prayer: adhan repetition is legislated but not iqamah (52), adhan is for notification (53), adhan for summoning, iqamah for commencement (54), quarter narrates completion (55), abundance defined by comparison (56), quarter stands for whole (57), leaving to back is not leaving (58). These maxims are used by Hanafi jurists to resolve new cases analogically.

Key Terms
تعارض الأدلة (taʿāruḍ al-adillah): Conflict of evidences; results in doubt requiring caution.
مشهور (mashhūr): Well-known hadith, transmitted by many but not reaching tawatur.
زيادة على الكتاب (ziyāda ʿalā al-kitāb): Addition to the Quran by way of sunnah, not contradiction.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim 37, what is the immediate result when there is a conflict of evidence regarding halal and haram?
A) The evidence that came first is followed.
B) It results in doubt.
C) The matter is considered permissible.
D) The matter is considered prohibited.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi maxims on evidence emphasize caution in doubt and recognize the authority of well-supported hadith practices.

Module 2 · Lesson 6

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
14 min
Maxims on Ability, Harm, and Legal Determinations
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi maxims regarding inability, harm removal, predominant opinion as certainty, and the rule that legal determinations prevent analogy.

Core Idea
Inability excuses; harm must be removed; predominant opinion holds weight; legal limits are fixed.

This lesson covers a set of maxims that deal with human capacity and the limits of law. Maxims 39-45 address the treatment of inability (sleeper, real incapacity), the removal of harm, and the principle that predominant opinion is like certainty. Maxim 48 is particularly important: 'The determination of the Law prevents attaching others to it' – meaning that specific quantities or durations set by shariah cannot be extended by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the treatment of inability
Maxim 39: Real inability must be considered. Maxim 40: A sleeping person is considered capable in estimation (taqdir) according to Abu Hanifa, meaning their actions may be valid if they later confirm intent.
This affects rulings on talaq, wudu, etc.
2
Apply the harm removal maxim
Maxim 45: Harm must be removed (al-darar yuzal). This is a universal maxim.
It underlies many concessions.
3
Learn about predominant opinion
Maxim 42: Ghalib al-ra'y (predominant opinion) is like certainty. This means in cases of doubt, if a strong probability exists, it is treated as certain.
Used in determining qibla direction, etc.
4
Grasp the limits of legal determinations
Maxim 48: The law's specific determinations (like waiting periods, shares) cannot be analogically extended. For example, the 'iddah of a divorced woman is fixed; you cannot analogize a different period.
This protects the text from excessive qiyas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

بَوْلَ مَا يُؤْكَلُ لَحْمُهُ طَاهِرٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ وَنَجِسٌ عِنْدَهُمَا (۲۹) إِنَّ التَّدَاوِى بِالْمُحْرِمِ لَا يَجُوزُ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ (٣٠) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِذَا عَادَلَ شَيْئًا يَأْخُذُ Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyyah) from the beginning of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are foundational principles that guide the derivation of rulings in various chapters of fiqh. The author presents them succinctly, often without proof, as they are axiomatic in the Hanafi school. The maxims cover diverse topics: disagreement of scholars brings ease (20), necessity dictates extent (21), benefit implies purity (22), achieving objective obviates extra conditions (23), tanning purifies skin (24), lifeless things do not decompose (25), well issues follow tradition not analogy (26), small amounts are excused (27), urine of edible animals is pure according to Imam Muhammad but impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (28), treatment with forbidden substances is prohibited (29), equality in cause gives same ruling (30), certainty not removed by doubt (31), things attributed to apparent cause (32), common origin gives same ruling (33), pure begets pure (34), inclusion by greater priority (35), impure begets impure (36), conflicting evidence on Halal and Haram brings doubt (37), well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran (38), established incapacity must be considered (39), sleeper considered capable in estimation (40), purification tools must be pure (41), predominant opinion like certainty (42), incapacity ruling only removed by certainty (43), no ability without knowledge (44), harm is removable (45), deviation from analogy follows textual detail (46), travel concession depends on travel (47), legal determinations prevent analogy (48), liquid removes impurity (49), impurity established by decisive proof is severe (50), conflicting texts on impurity bring ease (51). In the Book of Prayer: adhan repetition is legislated but not iqamah (52), adhan is for notification (53), adhan for summoning, iqamah for commencement (54), quarter narrates completion (55), abundance defined by comparison (56), quarter stands for whole (57), leaving to back is not leaving (58). These maxims are used by Hanafi jurists to resolve new cases analogically.

Key Terms
عجز (ʿajz): Inability; legally relevant if established in reality.
ضرر (ḍarar): Harm; must be removed by the least harmful means.
تقدير الشرع (taqdīr al-sharʿ): Specific determination by law (e.g., fixed shares, durations).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim 48, what is the ruling on extending a fixed legal quantity (e.g., a prescribed waiting period) by analogy?
A) It is allowed if the reason is similar.
B) It is not allowed, as the Law's determination prevents analogy.
C) It is allowed only with ijma.
D) It is compulsory to extend by analogy.

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh balances human capacity and textual boundaries through clear maxims on inability, harm, and legal determinations.

Maxims on Prayer and Severe Impurities
List of legal maxims with section headings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply Hanafi maxims on adhan, conditions of prayer, liquid as remover, and intensified impurities.

Core Idea
Adhan for notification; quarter stands for whole; liquid removes; severe impurity demands strictness.

This final lesson covers maxims from the Book of Prayer and additional purity rules. In prayer, maxims state that the adhan is for public announcement and the iqamah for starting the prayer; quarter of a thing can represent the whole (e.g., in covering). For impurities, liquid is considered a remover (like water washing), and impurities established by decisive proof are intensified (mughallazh), meaning stricter purification rules apply.

Guided Path
1
Understand the adhan and iqamah maxims
Maxims 52-54 clarify the purpose: adhan announces time, iqamah signals immediate start. Repetition of adhan is legislated but not of iqamah.
These are based on practice.
2
Learn about quarter standing for whole
Maxims 55-57: A quarter of something can represent the whole in certain rulings, like the minimum covering of 'awrah in prayer.
This is a pragmatic estimation.
3
Apply the liquid remover maxim
Maxim 49: A liquid (like water) is a remover of impurity. This means that if a liquid is pure, it can cleanse; if it is impure, it is a contaminant.
Distinguish from solids.
4
Identify severe impurities
Maxim 50: If impurity is established by a definitive proof (like Quran or mutawatir), it is intensified (mughallazh). E.g., pig and dog saliva.
Requires special purification like washing with soil.

الصَّحَابَةِ رَضِيَ اللهُ عنهم (۳۸) إِنَّ الْحَدِيث إِذَا كَانَ مَشْهُورًا وَعَمِلَتْ بِهِ الصَّحَابَةُ يَصِحُ بِهِ الزِّيَادَةُ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ باب التيمم (۳۹) إِنَّ الْعَجْزَ إِذَا كَانَ ثَابِتًا حَقِيْقَةً فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ اعْتِبَارِهِ (۴۰) إِنَّ النَّائِمَ قَادِرٌ تَقْدِيرًا عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ (۴۱) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ آلَةُ التَّطْهِيرِ فَلَا بُدَّ مِنْ طَهَارَتِهِ فِي نَفْسِهِ الضَّرَرَ مُسْقِط باب المسح على الخفين (٢٦) إِنَّ مَا هُوَ مَعْدُولٌ عَنِ الْقِيَاسِ يُرَاعَى جَمِيعُ مَا وَرَدَ بِهِ الشَّرُعُ (۴۷) إِنَّ رُخْصَةَ السَّفَرِ لَا تَبْقَى بِدُونِهِ باب الحيض والاستحاضة مُعَلَّظَةٌ (۵۱) إِنَّ تَعَارُضَ النَّصَّيْنِ فِى نَجَاسَةِ شَيْءٍ يُوجِبُ التَّخْفِيفَ عِندَ أَبِي حَنِيفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى كتاب الصلاة باب الأذان (۵۲) إِنَّ تَكْرَارَ الْأَذَانِ مَشْرُوعٌ دُونَ الْإِقَامَةِ (۵۳) إِنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ (۵۴) إِنَّ الأَدَانَ لِلاِسْتِحْضَارِ وَالْإِقَامَةَ لِإِعْلَامِ الْإِفْتِتَاحِ باب شروط الصلاة (۵۵) إِنَّ الرُّبُعَ يَحْكِي حِكَايَةَ الْكَمَالِ (۵۶) إِنَّ الشَّيْءَ إِنَّمَا يُوصَفُ بِالْكَبْرَةِ إِذَا كَانَ مَا يُقَابِلُهُ أَقَلَّ مِنْهُ (۵۷) إِنَّ رُبعَ الشَّيْءِ يَقُومُ مَقَامَ كُلِهِ (۵۸) إِنَّ تَرَكَ الشَّيْءِ إِلَى خَلْفِ لَا يَكُونُ تَرْعًا
Principles of Hidayah Volume 1 (20) Indeed, disagreement of scholars brings ease. (21) Indeed, when a matter is established by necessity, it is measured by its extent. (21) Indeed, that which is benefited from is not intrinsically impure. (23) Indeed, when the objective is achieved by something, there is no meaning to stipulating something else. (24) Indeed, that whose skin is purified by tanning is purified by zakat. (25) Indeed, a thing in which there is no life is not decomposed by death. Chapter on the Well (26) Indeed, the issues of wells are based on following traditions, not analogy. (27) Indeed, a small amount is excused due to necessity. (28) Indeed, the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten is pure according to Muhammad, and impure according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa). (29) Indeed, treatment with what is forbidden is not permissible according to Abu Hanifa. (30) Indeed, when a thing equals another, it takes its ruling. (31) Indeed, certainty is not removed by doubt. (32) Indeed, a thing, if it has an apparent cause, it is attributed to it. Chapter on Traces and Others (33) Indeed, when two things share the same origin and source, one takes the ruling of the other. (34) Indeed, what is generated from a pure thing is also pure. (35) Indeed, when a thing has a ruling, what is less than it enters that ruling by greater reason. (36) Indeed, what is generated from an impure thing is also impure. (37) Indeed, conflict of evidences regarding permissibility and prohibition brings doubt, and likewise disagreement of the Companions, may Allah be pleased with them. (38) Indeed, when a hadith is well-known and the Companions acted upon it, it is valid to add to the Quran by it. Chapter on Tayammum (39) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, it must be considered. (40) Indeed, a sleeping person is considered able in estimation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. (41) Indeed, that which is a means of purification must itself be pure. (42) Indeed, predominant opinion is like certainty. (43) Indeed, when inability is established in reality, its ruling does not cease except by a certainty like it. (44) No ability without knowledge. (45) Indeed, harm is removable. Chapter on Wiping over Khuffain (46) Indeed, what is deviated from analogy is observed according to all that the Law has brought. (47) Indeed, the concession of travel does not remain without it. Chapter on Menstruation and Istihadah (48) Indeed, the determination of the Law prevents attaching others to it. Chapter on Impurities and Their Purification (49) Indeed, a liquid is [a] remover. (50) Indeed, when impurity is established by a definitive proof, it is intensified. (51) Indeed, conflict of two texts regarding the impurity of something necessitates ease according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him. Book of Prayer Chapter on Adhan (52) Indeed, repetition of the adhan is legislated but not of the iqamah. (53) Indeed, the adhan is for notification. (54) Indeed, the adhan is for summoning and the iqamah is for announcing the commencement. Chapter on Conditions of Prayer (55) Indeed, the quarter narrates the narration of completion. (56) Indeed, a thing is only described as abundant when its opposite is less than it. (57) Indeed, a quarter of a thing stands in place of the whole. (58) Indeed, leaving a thing to the back is not a leaving.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage is a collection of Hanafi legal maxims (qawa'id fiqhiyyah) from the beginning of Usool al-Hidayah. These maxims are foundational principles that guide the derivation of rulings in various chapters of fiqh. The author presents them succinctly, often without proof, as they are axiomatic in the Hanafi school. The maxims cover diverse topics: disagreement of scholars brings ease (20), necessity dictates extent (21), benefit implies purity (22), achieving objective obviates extra conditions (23), tanning purifies skin (24), lifeless things do not decompose (25), well issues follow tradition not analogy (26), small amounts are excused (27), urine of edible animals is pure according to Imam Muhammad but impure according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (28), treatment with forbidden substances is prohibited (29), equality in cause gives same ruling (30), certainty not removed by doubt (31), things attributed to apparent cause (32), common origin gives same ruling (33), pure begets pure (34), inclusion by greater priority (35), impure begets impure (36), conflicting evidence on Halal and Haram brings doubt (37), well-known hadith acted upon by Companions can add to Quran (38), established incapacity must be considered (39), sleeper considered capable in estimation (40), purification tools must be pure (41), predominant opinion like certainty (42), incapacity ruling only removed by certainty (43), no ability without knowledge (44), harm is removable (45), deviation from analogy follows textual detail (46), travel concession depends on travel (47), legal determinations prevent analogy (48), liquid removes impurity (49), impurity established by decisive proof is severe (50), conflicting texts on impurity bring ease (51). In the Book of Prayer: adhan repetition is legislated but not iqamah (52), adhan is for notification (53), adhan for summoning, iqamah for commencement (54), quarter narrates completion (55), abundance defined by comparison (56), quarter stands for whole (57), leaving to back is not leaving (58). These maxims are used by Hanafi jurists to resolve new cases analogically.

Key Terms
مائع (māʾiʿ): Liquid; which removes impurity if pure.
نجاسة مغلظة (najāsa mughallaẓa): Intensified impurity requiring special purification (e.g., seven washes including soil).
ربع (rubʿ): Quarter; legally deemed sufficient to represent the whole in certain contexts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to maxim 50, what type of impurity requires intensified purification?
A) Any impurity proven by any hadith.
B) Impurity established by a definitive proof (dalīl maqtū‘ bihi).
C) Impurity that causes harm.
D) Impurity from animals.

Key Takeaway
Prayer and purity maxims provide specific rules for covering, adhan, and purification grades, reflecting Hanafi detail orientation.

Taharah — Purification

Legal Maxims (Qawa'id) from Usool al-Hidayah (Pages 4-5)
List of Hanafi legal maxims covering taharah and salah.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the meaning and fiqh application of each of the 40 Hanafi legal maxims listed in Usool al-Hidayah pages 4-5, and categorize them by topic (taharah, salah, etc.).

Core Idea
Maxims are the DNA of Hanafi fiqh—each one unlocks hundreds of rulings.

This passage from Usool al-Hidayah presents a collection of foundational legal maxims (qawa'id) used by the Hanafi school. They are organized by fiqh chapters and serve as mnemonic anchors for deriving and remembering rulings. In this lesson, we will work through each maxim, understand its meaning, and see how it applies to concrete cases in purity and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Scan Chapter Headings
Identify the major fiqh topics covered: general principles, wiping over socks, menstruation, impurities, adhan, conditions of prayer, description of prayer, recitation.
Maxims are grouped by chapter; this helps contextualize each one.
2
Parse Each Maxim in Arabic and Translation
Read the Arabic text and literal translation. Note any key terms like taqdir, rukhsah, or qiyas.
Pay attention to the numbering: some numbers are misread in OCR (e.g., ٢٦ for 46).
3
Identify the Core Legal Concept
For each maxim, pinpoint the central principle—e.g., maxim 40 deals with legal capacity (taqdir), maxim 45 with harm (darar).
These concepts often appear across multiple fiqh chapters.
4
Relate to a Concrete Fiqh Ruling
Give a simple example from Hanafi fiqh. For maxim 40: a sleeping person's wudu is valid when he moves in sleep. For maxim 47: travel concessions end when travel ends.
Use examples from the chapter headings when possible.
5
Connect to Madhhab Methodology
Explain how the maxim reflects Hanafi usul—e.g., istihsan, taqdir, or the role of customary practice (urf).
Some maxims have intra-madhhab variations (e.g., Abu Hanifa vs. the two companions).

(۵۳) إِنَّ الْأَذَانَ لِلْإِعْلَامِ

(۶۵) إِنَّ رَفْعَ الْيَدِ لِإِعْلَامِ الْأَصَمِّ
(۲۶) إِنَّ التَّكْبِيرَ هُوَ التَّعْظِيمُ لُغَةً
(۲۷) إِنَّ لُغَةَ الْعَرَبِ لَهَا مِنَ الْمَزِيَّةِ مَا لَيْسَ لِغَيْرِهَا
(۲۸) إِنَّ فِي الْأَذَانِ يُعْتَبَرُ التَّعَارُفُ
(۲۹) إِنَّ كُلَّ قِيَامٍ فِيْهِ ذِكْرُ مَسْئُونٍ يُعْتَمَدُ فِيْهِ وَمَا لَا فَلَا
(۷۰) إِنَّ التَّعَوُّدَ تَبَعٌ لِلْقِرَاءَةِ دُونَ الثَّنَاءِ عِندَ الطَّرَفَيْنِ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ
(۷۱) إِنَّ الزِّيَادَةَ عَلَى الْكِتَابِ بِخَبَرِ الْوَاحِدِ لَا يَجُوزُ لَكِنَّهُ يُوجِبُ الْعَمَلَ
(۷۲) إِنَّ مَبْنَى الدُّعَاءِ عَلَى الْإِخْفَاءِ
(۷۳) إِنَّ الصَّلَاةَ مَا وُضِعَتْ لِلِاسْتِرَاحَةِ
(۷۴) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ عَلَى الْبَدَنِ أَشَقُّ أَوْلَى
(۷۵) إِنَّ مَا لَا يَسْتَحِيلُ سُؤَالُهُ مِنَ الْعِبَادِ يَشْبَهُ كَلَامَ النَّاسِ وَيَسْتَحِيلُ لَيْسَ مِنْ كَلَامِهِمْ

(۷) إِنَّ التَّخْسِيرَ يُنَافِى الْفَرْضِيَّةَ وَالْوُجُوبَ
فصل في القراءة
(۷۸) إِنَّ مَا كَانَ مُكَمِّلًا لِشَيْءٍ فَهُوَ تَابِعٌ لَهُ
(۷۹) إِنَّ الْجَهْرَ يَخْتَصُّ إِمَّا بِالْجَمَاعَةِ حَتْمًا أَوْ بِالْوَقْتِ فِي حَقِّ الْمُنْفَرِدِ عَلَى وَجْهِ التَّخْسِيرِ
(40) The sleeping person is deemed capable by estimation according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him.
(41) Whatever is an instrument of purification, its own cleanliness is necessary.
(42) Prevailing opinion is like certainty.
(43) When inability is established as a fact, its ruling does not disappear except by a similar certainty.
(44) There is no capability without knowledge.
(45) Harm is removed.
Chapter: Wiping over leather socks
(46) Whatever is deviated from analogy, all that has come in the sacred law is observed.
(47) The concession of travel does not remain without it.
Chapter: Menstruation and Istihadah
(48) The determination of the sacred law prevents attaching other things to it.
Chapter: Impurities and their purification
(49) Liquid is a remover.
(50) When impurity of a thing is established by conclusive evidence, it is severe.
(51) The conflict of two texts regarding the impurity of a thing necessitates leniency according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah the Exalted have mercy on him.
Book of Prayer

(52) Repetition of the adhan is prescribed, not of the iqamah.
(53) The adhan is for notification.
(54) The adhan is for summoning and the iqamah is for announcing the commencement.
Chapter: Conditions of Prayer
(55) The quarter relates the relation of completeness.
(56) A thing is described as abundant only when its counterpart is less than it.
(57) A quarter of a thing takes the place of its whole.
(58) Abandoning a thing to a successor is not abandonment.
(59) Obligation is according to capacity.
(60) Inquiry is above conjecture.
(61) Acting upon ijtihad for the future is obligatory without invalidating what was performed before.
Chapter: Description of Prayer
(62) The term sunnah may be applied to what is proven obligatory by the Sunnah.
(63) Conjunction necessitates differentiation.
(64) Negation takes precedence over affirmation.
(65) Raising the hand is for informing the deaf.
(66) Takbir linguistically means magnification.
(67) The Arabic language has a virtue that other languages do not have.
(68) In the adhan, customary recognition is considered.
(69) Every standing in which there is remembrance of a requested matter is relied upon, and what does not have such is not.
(70) Seeking refuge (ta'awwudh) follows the recitation, not the praise (thana'), according to the two shaykhs, may Allah have mercy on them.
(71) Addition to the Book by a solitary report is not permissible, but it necessitates action.
(72) Supplication is based on concealment.
(73) Prayer was not established for rest.
(74) What is harder on the body is more deserving.
(75) What it is not impossible to ask from people resembles human speech, and it is impossible for it not to be from their speech.

(78) Whatever is a complement to something is subordinate to it.
(79) Recitation aloud is specific either to the congregation necessarily or to the time in the case of the individual, by way of specification.

Commentary
This passage presents a collection of legal maxims (qawa'id) from the Hanafi school, as compiled in the work 'Usool al-Hidayah'. Each maxim is a foundational principle that guides legal reasoning in various chapters of fiqh. The maxims are numbered and organized under the relevant fiqh topics: purity (taharah), prayer (salah), and subdivisions such as wiping over socks, menstruation, impurities, adhan, conditions of prayer, description of prayer, and recitation. The maxims cover both substantive rulings (like the legal capacity of a sleeping person) and principles of interpretation (like the precedence of negation over affirmation). The commentary should explain the context of each maxim within the Hanafi school, but due to space, a general explanation is given: these maxims are derived from the Quran, Sunnah, and the ijtihad of the early Hanafi imams, particularly Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. They serve as mnemonic devices to remember key legal principles.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'idah): A foundational legal principle from which multiple rulings are derived.
تقدير (taqdir): Legal estimation; attributing a ruling to a person based on a presumed capacity.
رخصة السفر (rukhsat al-safar): The legal concession granted to a traveler, such as shortening or combining prayers.
غالب الرأي (ghalib al-ra'y): Prevailing opinion; a high degree of probability treated as certainty for legal purposes.
ضرر (darar): Harm or injury, which must be removed or prevented in Islamic law.

Tayammum: Absolute Purification or Necessity Concession?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the nature of tayammum

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on the nature of tayammum and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) regarding the validity of prayer when water appears mid-prayer.

Core Idea
Tayammum's legal nature determines whether prayer remains valid if water appears mid-prayer.

Tayammum is a dry ablution performed when water is unavailable. While all Hanafi scholars agree on its permissibility in necessity, they differ on its legal effect: does it genuinely remove ritual impurity (like wudu) or merely provide a temporary concession? This brief passage introduces the intra-Hanafi debate between the Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) and Muhammad al-Shaybani, and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions
Locate the two terms in the passage: 'tahara mutlaqa' (absolute purification) held by the Shaykhayn, and 'tahara daruriyya' (necessity purification) held by Muhammad.
These terms capture the essence of the dispute.
2
Understand the core of the dispute
The difference is about whether tayammum actually removes hadath (ritual impurity) or merely permits prayer as a concession as long as the excuse lasts.
3
Examine the practical consequence
The key test case: if a person in tayammum sees water during prayer, Abu Hanifa says the prayer is valid, Muhammad says it becomes invalid. This is the thamarah al-khilaf.
Many other subsidiary issues branch from this difference.
4
Note the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that of Abu Hanifa (tahara mutlaqa). Later Hanafi authorities favor this view.
In fatwa, the prayer is considered valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ التَّيَمُّمَ طَهَارَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ عِندَ الشَّيْخَيْنِ رَحِمَهُمَا اللَّهُ وَطَهَارَةٌ ضَرُورِيَّةٌ عِنْدَ مُحَمَّدٍ رَحِمَهُ اللهُ
Verily, tayammum is an absolute purification (tahara mutlaqa) according to the two Shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), may Allah have mercy on them, and a necessity purification (tahara daruriyya) according to Muhammad, may Allah have mercy on him.
Source pages p. 6

Commentary
This is a well-known difference between the early Hanafi imams regarding the nature of tayammum (dry ablution). According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Shaykhayn), tayammum is a 'mutlaqa' (absolute) purification, meaning it removes impurity (hadath) just like wudu does, but limited to the purpose. According to Muhammad al-Shaybani, tayammum is a 'daruriyya' (necessity-based) purification, meaning it only permits the prayer at that moment but does not actually remove impurity; it is a concession that subsists only as long as the excuse persists. This difference affects several subsidiary issues: for example, if a person in tayammum sees water during prayer, according to Abu Hanifa the prayer is valid (since his tayammum was true purification), while according to Muhammad the prayer breaks (since the concession ended). The mufta bihi position is that of Abu Hanifa (tahara mutlaqa) in most cases.

Key Terms
طَهَارَةٌ مُطْلَقَةٌ (ṭahāra mutlaqa): Absolute purification: tayammum fully removes ritual impurity for the purpose of prayer.
طَهَارَةٌ ضَرُورِيَّةٌ (ṭahāra ḍarūriyya): Necessity purification: tayammum only permits prayer under duress, does not actually remove impurity.
التَّيَمُّمُ (al-tayammum): Dry ablution performed with clean earth when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, what is the legal nature of tayammum?
A) A necessity purification (tahara daruriyya).
B) An absolute purification (tahara mutlaqa).
C) A symbolic purification.
D) Not a valid purification.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school has two valid positions on tayammum, but the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) considers it an absolute purification that renders prayer valid even if water appears mid-prayer.

Intention Must Accompany Action
States condition for valid intention.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the condition of ittisal for valid intention and IDENTIFY the exception for fasting.

Core Idea
Intention must immediately precede the action – delay invalidates the worship.

This short principle from the Hidayah is a foundational rule for all acts of worship except where a specific dispensation exists. In this lesson, you will learn what 'ittisal' means and how it applies to wudu, salah, and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
Read the Arabic statement: intention is valid only if connected to the action. This is a condition (shart) for most acts of worship.
The ruling is categorical: if not connected, the intention is invalid.
2
Define 'ittisal'
'Ittisal' means temporal contiguity: the intention must be made at the very start of the act, without any gap. For example, in wudu, the intention is made when washing the first part of the body (the face).
This differs from general 'niyyah' which can precede actions like fasting.
3
Apply to specific acts
For wudu and salah, the intention must accompany the opening act. For salah, it is made when saying the takbir. For zakat, it can be made when setting aside the wealth.
The rule ensures mindfulness at the outset.
4
Identify the exception
Fasting is an exception: intention can be made at night or before dawn, even if not immediately connected to the act of fasting (which begins at dawn).
This is due to the extended duration of fasting.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ النِّيَّةَ إِنِ اتَّصَلَتْ بِالْعَمَلِ وَإِلَّا فَلَا
Indeed, intention: if it is connected to the action, then (it is valid); otherwise, not.
Source pages p. 9

Commentary
This principle concerns the timing of niyyah (intention) for acts of worship like wudu, prayer, fasting. The intention must be made at the beginning of the act, without a gap. For example, for wudu, intention should be made when washing the face. If one delays intention until after the act is partly done, it is not valid. However, for some acts like fasting, the intention can be made at night or before dawn.

Key Terms
اتَّصَلَتْ (ittaṣalat): Connected or contiguous in time, meaning the intention immediately precedes the action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
For wudu, when must the intention be made?
A) Any time during wudu
B) At the start of washing the face
C) After completion
D) Before starting

Key Takeaway
Intention must be made at the beginning of an act of worship to be valid; fasting is an exception.

The Lesser Follows the Greater
Legal maxim from Usool al-Hidayah, Taharah chapter.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim 'Inna al-qalīla tābi‘un li al-akthar', explain its meaning, and apply it to a case of mixed water purity.

Core Idea
The ruling of the majority determines the whole — the lesser is subordinate to the greater.

This lesson presents a foundational Hanafi legal maxim from the chapter on purification (tahārah). Understanding this maxim will help you assess the purity of water when a small amount of impurity or pure substance mixes with a larger quantity. The maxim is not about counting heads but about the legal weight of quantities.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the Arabic text
Learn the exact wording: 'إِنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ تَابِعٌ لِلْاكُثَرِ'. This is a concise legal axiom that will recur in many fiqh rulings.
Focus on the contrast between 'qalīl' (little) and 'akthar' (more).
2
Understand the lexical meaning
'Inna' is an emphasis. 'Al-qalīl' means the small quantity; 'tābi‘un' means following/subordinate; 'li al-akthar' means to the greater. The literal translation: 'Indeed, the little is a follower of the greater.'
3
Grasp the legal principle
This maxim states that when two entities or quantities are mixed, the ruling of the dominant (greater) prevails over the subordinate (lesser). In practice, if a small amount of impure water mixes with a large amount of pure water, the mixture takes the ruling of the pure water (provided the impurity is not dominant).
This is not about majority opinion but about quantitative or qualitative weight.
4
Apply to a concrete fiqh case
Consider two water containers: one contains 10 litres of pure water, the other contains 0.5 litres of water with a minor impurity. If they mix, the total is 10.5 litres. Since the pure water is the majority (akthar), the mixture is considered pure (tāhir) according to this maxim.
This is a simplified example; actual fiqh rules consider the nature of the impurity and the quantity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إِنَّ الْقَلِيْلَ تَابِعٌ لِلْاكُثَرِ
Indeed, the little is a follower of the greater.
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This is a legal maxim (qā‘idah fiqhiyyah) from the Hanafi school, typically used in rulings on purity (tahārah). For example, if a small amount of water becomes mixed with a large amount of pure water, the ruling of the larger quantity prevails. The principle is that a ruling is determined by the majority, not the minority.

Key Terms
الْقَلِيْلَ (al-qalīl): The small part or quantity, as opposed to the majority.
تَابِعٌ (tābi‘): Follower or subordinate; the legal ruling of the minor part follows that of the major part.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the maxim 'Inna al-qalīla tābi‘un li al-akthar,' what happens if a small amount of unclean water mixes with a large amount of clean water?
A) The water becomes impure.
B) The water remains pure.
C) The water becomes makruh.
D) The ruling depends on intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'The lesser follows the greater' teaches us that when a small quantity is mixed with a large one, the ruling of the majority prevails, especially in matters of purity.
